         <div class="date-outer">
          <h2 class="date-header">
           <span>
            Tuesday, July 07, 2015
           </span>
          </h2>
          <div class="date-posts">
           <div class="post-outer">
            <div class="post hentry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
             <meta content="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Russell_square_ambulances.jpg/100px-Russell_square_ambulances.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
             <meta content="29101447" itemprop="blogId"/>
             <meta content="2344133952577169185" itemprop="postId"/>
             <a name="2344133952577169185">
             </a>
             <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
              <a href="http://conservativeweasel.blogspot.com.au/2015/07/tue-jul-7th-todays-news.html">
               Tue Jul 7th Todays News
              </a>
             </h3>
             <div class="post-header">
              <div class="post-header-line-1">
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2344133952577169185" itemprop="articleBody">
              <span style="background-color: white; font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                <span style="line-height: 19px;">
                 At last you can revel in the joys of smaller government on this site for the
                 <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/theboltreport/" style="color: #de7008;">
                  Bolt Report Supporter's Group
                 </a>
                 onFacebook. If something is broke, you fix it. Or not. There won't be any purges or changes because I've not the time to do much. But if you do something outrageous which I must respond to I will.
                </span>
               </span>
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               ===
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               Greece is a warning to Australia of what will happen if cuts to spending are not made. The extremist left wing government of Greece has made many promises they cannot keep. The spending is so big, the debt is so substantial they cannot meet loan repayments even with international help. Expenses include welfare. Greeks have to work to make up for the things that their elders took without paying. There are two paths Greece can take. The left wing path which involves trashing everything Greece has and prospering through poverty and misery until the debt is forgotten. The conservative path is to take ownership of the debt and pay it off through prudent cuts and hard work.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <br/>
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               Same Sex Marriage is shown to be a Trojan Horse by various groups keen to hurt Christian Churches, suing them to perform marriages they are unwilling through conscience to
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               commit. Also, extremist advocates are pursuing marriage for very young. Or, marriage for very many. Already, Australia recognises polygamy through overseas jurisdictions, and some migrants or refugees who have obtained welfare have had such unions recognised in payments.However arrangements can be made where churches are not threatened and those avenues can be pursued.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               <br/>
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               Globalwarmists failed to predict cold weather. A thirty year record for cool weather has struck Sydney this winter. It continues unabated.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               <br/>
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               Australia does not need an apartheid constitution, but many are advocating it, including those who would be victim to it. Changing the constitution is notmeaningless and recognising race is not benign by the state. The state is not an apologist of history, although it is a historical document. Australia is not owned by
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               Aborigines, Irish or Greeks. Australia belongs to those not yet born, or vey young. We adults have her in trust for them.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               <br/>
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               Mr Shorten has to explain to the Royal Commission matters which have been obscured by missing material. Documents regarding thearrangements of payments for and by union members have been lost after a transfer to electronic systems. Shorten needs to explain why his union behaved as a bastard employer, cutting member benefits for apparently, corruptly obtained money.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <br/>
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               Australian Broadcasting Corporation (ABC) is out of control. She is not answerable to anyone for over a $billion each year. She hasfour tv channels and numerous radio and internet ports, making her the largest media body in Australia. Publicly paid for and with advantages smaller private media do not have. She is partisan. Her component journalists are overwhelmingly left wing, more than a third extremist Green. The only identifiable conservative was in fact Green. ABC has set up an audit following her hiring a jihadist to attack the government by ambush.
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               Ray Martin has prejudiced the audit he was appointed to independently run, claiming his audit will be about proving balance. Proving balance is not the function of an audit. One example of a p
              </span>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               ress double standard is reporting re Gillian Triggs. Triggs is head of the Human Rights Commission and is paid $400k a year. Of all the other HRC members, all are extreme left, except one recently appointed (not conservative) Libertarian, Wilson. Wilson's expenses were tabled recently. They are commensurate with Triggs, whose expenses had not been tabled by the media.
              </span>
              <br/>
              <br/>
              <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
               In 1124,
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon">
                Tyre
               </a>
               fell to the
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusaders">
                Crusaders
               </a>
               . 1456, A
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrial_of_Joan_of_Arc">
                retrial verdict
               </a>
               acquitted
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_of_Arc">
                Joan of Arc
               </a>
               of
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy_in_Christianity">
                heresy
               </a>
               25 years after her death. 1520, Spanish
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquistador">
                conquistadores
               </a>
               defeated a larger
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aztec_Triple_Alliance">

               </a>
               army at the
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Otumba">
                Battle of Otumba
               </a>
               . About 1000 faced as many as 40,000, conceding 73 deaths to as many as 20,000. 1534,
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas">
                European colonization of the Americas
               </a>
               : First known exchange between Europeans and natives of the
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence">

               </a>
               in
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Brunswick">
                New Brunswick
               </a>

               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg">
                Luxembourg
               </a>

               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raid_of_the_Redeswire">
                Raid of the Redeswire
               </a>
               , the last major battle between
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_England">
                England
               </a>
               and
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland">
                Scotland
               </a>
               . It wasn't a raid. It wasn't fought in or over Redeswire, and it wasn't between England and Scotland but over a disagreement between an Englishman and a Scot, both of whomcould afford armies. The Scot defeated a dishonourable man. 1585, the
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Nemours">

               </a>
               abolished tolerance to
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestantism">

               in France. 1770, the
               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Larga">

               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress">

               <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-War">

               </a>
               ". The US had been upset by the behaviour of revolutionary France. They sent a delegationgo three, but French diplomats insisted on bribes. Two delegates returned to the US and the correspondence, including the bribe demands, were made public. Francophile Jefferson didn't see a problem.

                  <div>
                   <div style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; text-align: center;">
                    <span style="font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                     2014
                    </span>
                   </div>
                   <div>
                    <div style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      Former Australian PM Malcolm Fraser has invoked the name of Hitler in describing the new government's successful immigration program and border protection. New parliamentarian and former rich man Clive Palmer has called Queensland Premier Campbell Newman a Nazi. The denunciations are hyperbolic. It is a good thing that people are not drowning trying to start a new life in Australia. Australia is a good place for a new life, but one doesn't want to die coming here, or be exploited by pirates. Fraser had few problems drowning Vietnamese peoples or leaving Zimbabwe peoples at the mercy of a murderous dictator. Palmer is the former campaign manager of Joh Bjelke Peterson .. it is not the case he means what he says all the time, or any time. So what is behind their criticism? Those who are hard core ALP or Green supporters like the sound of the waffle.
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      A lot of violence is related to bikies, drugs and organised crime. So it is sadly depressing when a casual murder takes place in a popular shopping mall during the school holidays and it has nothing to do with anything, but a likely dispute over a woman between rivals. Herodotus was dismissive of the Greeks sailing ten thousand ships to regain Helen of Troy. Instead of fighting their rivals, they should be trying to impress the girl. I doubt she is impressed at what happened, the two argued over a cosmetics counter and one stabbed the other multiple times in the chest, and left the knife in the chest of his dying rival, lit a
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      cigarette and waited for police. A chilling and casual murder which can not be tolerated, but must accrue a life term in jail, there being no excuse or alternative. The imaginary Sherlock finding Moriarty excuse not meeting a modern legal standard.
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      Issues of justice arise on this day. In 1456, Joan of Arc was acquitted of heresy twenty five years after she was murdered for it. In 1585, the treaty of Nemours meant a policy of tolerance ended. In 1798, US Congress voted to end peace with France. In 1834, fournights of rioting against abolitionists in NYC began on this day. In 1846, US troops began toacquire California from Mexico. The US attempted the draft in 1863, offering exemptions for $300. Two years later, four conspirators were hung for the killing of Lincoln. But today is not entirely without mercy or grace. In 1928, sliced bread was sold forthe first time, on the inventor's 48th birthday. In 1954, Elvis made his radio debut. In 1983, a thirteen year old girl became an ambassador for the US in the Soviet Union. It is the birthday of Mahler (1860), Heinlein (1907), Eddings (1931), Ringo Starr (1940) and Bill Oddie (1941)
                     </span>
                    </div>
                    <div>
                     <div style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
                      <div style="text-align: center;">
                       <span style="font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: medium;">
                        Historical perspectives on this day
                       </span>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1124,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon">
                       Tyre
                      </a>
                      fell to the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusaders">
                       Crusaders
                      </a>
                      . 1456, A
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrial_of_Joan_of_Arc">
                       retrial verdict
                      </a>
                      acquitted
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_of_Arc">
                       Joan of Arc
                      </a>
                      of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy_in_Christianity">
                       heresy
                      </a>
                      25 years after her death. 1520, Spanish
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquistador">
                       conquistadores
                      </a>
                      defeated a larger
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aztec_Triple_Alliance">
                       Aztec
                      </a>
                      army at the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Otumba">
                       Battle of Otumba
                      </a>
                      . 1534,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas">
                       European colonization of the Americas
                      </a>
                      : First known exchange between Europeans and natives of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence">
                       Gulf of St. Lawrence
                      </a>
                      in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Brunswick">
                       New Brunswick
                      </a>
                      . 1543, French troops invaded
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg">
                       Luxembourg
                      </a>
                      . 1575,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raid_of_the_Redeswire">
                       Raid of the Redeswire
                      </a>
                      , the last major battle between
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_England">
                       England
                      </a>
                      and
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland">
                       Scotland
                      </a>
                      . 1585, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Nemours">
                       Treaty of Nemours
                      </a>
                      abolished tolerance to
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestantism">
                       Protestants
                      </a>
                      in France. 1770, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Larga">
                       Battle of Larga
                      </a>
                      between the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire">
                       Russian Empire
                      </a>
                      and the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire">
                       Ottoman Empire
                      </a>
                      took place. 1777,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War">
                       American Revolutionary War
                      </a>
                      : American forces retreating from
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Ticonderoga">
                       Fort Ticonderoga
                      </a>
                      were defeated in the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Hubbardton">
                       Battle of Hubbardton
                      </a>
                      . 1798, as a result of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XYZ_Affair">
                       XYZ Affair
                      </a>
                      , the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress">
                       U.S. Congress
                      </a>
                      rescinded the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Alliance_(1778)">
                       Treaty of Alliance
                      </a>
                      with France sparking the "
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-War">
                       Quasi-War
                      </a>
                      ".
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1807,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars">
                       Napoleonic Wars
                      </a>
                      : The
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit">
                       Peace of Tilsit
                      </a>
                      between France,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia">
                       Prussia
                      </a>
                      and Russia ended the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition">
                       War of the Fourth Coalition
                      </a>
                      . 1834, in New York City,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abolitionist_riots_(1834)">
                       four nights of rioting
                      </a>
                      against
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States">
                       abolitionists
                      </a>
                      began. 1846,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War">
                       MexicanAmerican War
                      </a>
                      : American troops occupied
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monterey,_California">
                       Monterey
                      </a>
                      and
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco">
                       Yerba Buena
                      </a>
                      , thus beginning the U.S. acquisition of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California">
                       California
                      </a>
                      . 1863, United States began its first
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription">
                       military draft
                      </a>
                      ; exemptions cost $300. 1865,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War">
                       American Civil War
                      </a>
                      : Four conspirators in the assassination of President
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln">
                       Abraham Lincoln
                      </a>
                      were hanged. 1892,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katipunan">
                       Katipunan
                      </a>
                      : The Revolutionary Philippine Brotherhood was established, contributing to the fall of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Empire">
                       Spanish Empire
                      </a>
                      in Asia. 1898,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States">
                       U.S. President
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_McKinley">
                       William McKinley
                      </a>
                      signed the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newlands_Resolution">
                       Newlands Resolution
                      </a>
                      annexing Hawaii as a territory of the United States.
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1907,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florenz_Ziegfeld,_Jr.">
                       Florenz Ziegfeld, Jr.
                      </a>
                      staged his first
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ziegfeld_Follies">
                       Follies
                      </a>
                      on the roof of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bowery_Theatre">
                       New York Theater
                      </a>
                      in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City">
                       New York City
                      </a>
                      . 1911, the United States, Great Britain, Japan, and Russia signed the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Pacific_Fur_Seal_Convention_of_1911">
                       North Pacific Fur Seal Convention of 1911
                      </a>
                      banning open-water
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seal_hunting">
                       seal hunting
                      </a>
                      , the first international treaty to address wildlife preservation issues. 1915,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I">
                       World War I
                      </a>
                      : End of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Battle_of_the_Isonzo">
                       First Battle of the Isonzo
                      </a>
                      . Also 1915, an
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Railway_(New_York_%E2%80%93_Ontario)">
                       International Railway
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tram">
                       trolley
                      </a>
                      with an extreme overload of 157 passengers crashed near
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queenston,_Ontario">
                       Queenston, Ontario
                      </a>
                      , killing 15. Also 1915, Militia officer
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Pedris">
                       Henry Pedris
                      </a>
                      was executed by firing squad at
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colombo">
                       Colombo
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka">
                       Ceylon
                      </a>
                      - an act widely regarded as a miscarriage of justice by the British colonial authorities. 1928,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sliced_bread">
                       Sliced bread
                      </a>
                      was sold for the first time (on
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Frederick_Rohwedder">
                       the inventor's
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_7#Births">
                       48th birthday
                      </a>
                      ) by the Chillicothe Baking Company of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chillicothe,_Missouri">
                       Chillicothe, Missouri
                      </a>
                      .
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1930, industrialist
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_J._Kaiser">
                       Henry J. Kaiser
                      </a>
                      began construction of the Boulder Dam (now known as
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoover_Dam">
                       Hoover Dam
                      </a>
                      ). 1937,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War">
                       Second Sino-Japanese War
                      </a>
                      :
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_Incident">
                       Battle of Lugou Bridge
                      </a>
                      : Japanese forces invaded Beijing, China. 1941,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II">
                       World War II
                      </a>
                      : U.S. forces landed in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iceland">
                       Iceland
                      </a>
                      , taking over from an earlier British occupation. 1941, World War II:
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beirut">
                       Beirut
                      </a>
                      was occupied by
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_French_Forces">
                       Free France
                      </a>
                      and British troops. 1944, World War II: Largest
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banzai_charge">
                       Banzai charge
                      </a>
                      of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_War">
                       Pacific War
                      </a>
                      at the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Saipan">
                       Battle of Saipan
                      </a>
                      . 1946, Mother
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francesca_S._Cabrini">
                       Francesca S. Cabrini
                      </a>
                      became the first American to be canonised. Also 1946,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howard_Hughes">
                       Howard Hughes
                      </a>
                      nearly died when his
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hughes_XF-11">
                       XF-11
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft">
                       reconnaissance aircraft
                      </a>
                      prototype crashed in a
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California">
                       Beverly Hills
                      </a>
                      neighbourhood. 1947, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roswell_incident">
                       Roswell incident
                      </a>
                      , the (supposed) crash of an
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life">
                       alien
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spaceship">
                       spaceship
                      </a>
                      near
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roswell,_New_Mexico">
                       Roswell
                      </a>
                      in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Mexico">
                       New Mexico
                      </a>
                      .
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1952, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ocean_liner">
                       ocean liner
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SS_United_States">
                       SS United States
                      </a>
                      passed
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bishop_Rock,_Isles_of_Scilly">
                       Bishop Rock
                      </a>
                      on her maiden voyage, breaking the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Riband">
                       transatlantic speed record
                      </a>
                      to become the fastest passenger ship in the world. 1953,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara">
                       Ernesto "Che" Guevara
                      </a>
                      set out on a
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara#Guatemala.2C_Arbenz_and_United_Fruit">
                       trip
                      </a>
                      through
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolivia">
                       Bolivia
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peru">
                       Peru
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecuador">
                       Ecuador
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panama">
                       Panama
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Costa_Rica">
                       Costa Rica
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicaragua">
                       Nicaragua
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honduras">
                       Honduras
                      </a>
                      , and
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Salvador">
                       El Salvador
                      </a>
                      . 1954,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elvis_Presley">
                       Elvis Presley
                      </a>
                      made his radio debut when WHBQ Memphis played his first recording for Sun Records, "That's All Right." 1956,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fritz_Moravec">
                       Fritz Moravec
                      </a>
                      and two other Austrian mountaineers made the first ascent of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gasherbrum_II">
                       Gasherbrum II
                      </a>
                      (8,035 m). 1958, U.S. President
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower">
                       Dwight D. Eisenhower
                      </a>
                      signed the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Statehood_Act">
                       Alaska Statehood Act
                      </a>
                      into
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_the_United_States">
                       law
                      </a>
                      . 1959,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus">
                       Venus
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occultation">
                       occult
                      </a>
                      ed the star
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regulus">
                       Regulus
                      </a>
                      . This rare event was used to determine the diameter of Venus and the structure of the Venusian atmosphere. 1963,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_crisis">
                       Buddhist crisis
                      </a>
                      : The police of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Nhu">
                       Ng nh Nhu
                      </a>
                      , brother and chief political adviser of President
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Di%E1%BB%87m">
                       Ng nh Dim
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Seven_Day_scuffle">
                       attacked
                      </a>
                      a group of American journalists who were covering a protest. 1978, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon_Islands">
                       Solomon Islands
                      </a>
                      became independent from the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom">
                       United Kingdom
                      </a>
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      In 1980, institution of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia">
                       sharia
                      </a>
                      in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran">
                       Iran
                      </a>
                      . Also 1980, during the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War">
                       Lebanese Civil War
                      </a>
                      , 83
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigers_Militia">
                       Tiger
                      </a>
                      militants were killed during what would be known as the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safra_massacre">
                       Safra massacre
                      </a>
                      . 1981,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States">
                       U.S. President
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan">
                       Ronald Reagan
                      </a>
                      appointed
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandra_Day_O%27Connor">
                       Sandra Day O'Connor
                      </a>
                      to become the first female member of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States">
                       Supreme Court of the United States
                      </a>
                      . 1983,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War">
                       Cold War
                      </a>
                      :
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samantha_Smith">
                       Samantha Smith
                      </a>
                      , a U.S. schoolgirl, flew to the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union">
                       Soviet Union
                      </a>
                      at the invitation of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_the_Soviet_Union">
                       Secretary General
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Andropov">
                       Yuri Andropov
                      </a>
                      . 1985,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Becker">
                       Boris Becker
                      </a>
                      became the youngest player ever to win
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon">
                       Wimbledon
                      </a>
                      at age 17. 1991,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars">
                       Yugoslav Wars
                      </a>
                      : The
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brijuni_Agreement">
                       Brioni Agreement
                      </a>
                      ended the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ten-Day_War">
                       ten-day independence war
                      </a>
                      in
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovenia">
                       Slovenia
                      </a>
                      against the rest of the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia">
                       Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia
                      </a>
                      . 1997, the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces">
                       Turkish Armed Forces
                      </a>
                      withdrew from northern
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq">
                       Iraq
                      </a>
                      after
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Hammer_(1997)">
                       assisting
                      </a>
                      the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Democratic_Party">
                       Kurdistan Democratic Party
                      </a>
                      in the
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_Kurdish_Civil_War">
                       Iraqi Kurdish Civil War
                      </a>
                      . 2003,
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA">
                       NASA
                      </a>
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opportunity_rover">
                       Opportunity rover
                      </a>
                      , MER-B or Mars Exploration RoverB, was launched into space aboard a
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delta_II">
                       Delta II
                      </a>
                      rocket. 2005, a series of
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings">
                       four explosions
                      </a>
                      occurred on
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transport_in_London">
                       London's transport system
                      </a>
                      killing 56 people including four
                      <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suicide_bombers">
                       suicide bombers
                      </a>
                      and injuring over 700 others.
                     </span>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                  </div>

                             , Japanese singer (

                           Independence Day
                          </a>
                          in the
                          <b>
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon_Islands" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Solomon Islands">

                           </a>
                          </b>

                           1978
                          </a>
                          )

                         <div id="mp-otd-img" style="float: right; font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; margin-left: 0.5em;">
                          <div style="line-height: inherit; margin-bottom: 0.5em; margin-top: 0.5em;">
                           <a class="image" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Russell_square_ambulances.jpg" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Ambulances at Russell Square, London, after the 7 July 2005 bombings">

                           </a>

                         </div>
                         <ul style="font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; line-height: 22px; list-style-image: url(data:image/svg+xml,%3C%3Fxml%20version%3D%221.0%22%20encoding%3D%22UTF-8%22%3F%3E%0A%3Csvg%20xmlns%3D%22http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg%22%20version%3D%221.1%22%20width%3D%225%22%20height%3D%2213%22%3E%0A%3Ccircle%20cx%3D%222.5%22%20cy%3D%229.5%22%20r%3D%222.5%22%20fill%3D%22%2300528c%22%2F%3E%0A%3C%2Fsvg%3E%0A); margin: 0.3em 0px 0px 1.6em; padding: 0px;">
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1456" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1456">
                            1456
                           </a>
                            Twenty-five years after her death,
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Joan of Arc">
                            Joan of Arc
                           </a>
                           was
                           <b>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrial_of_Joan_of_Arc" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Retrial of Joan of Arc">
                             declared innocent
                            </a>
                           </b>
                           of heresy in a
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Posthumous_trial" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Posthumous trial">
                            posthumous retrial
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1834" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1834">
                            1834
                           </a>
                            In New York City,
                           <b>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-abolitionist_riots_(1834)" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Anti-abolitionist riots (1834)">
                             four nights of rioting
                            </a>
                           </b>
                           against
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Abolitionism">
                            abolitionists
                           </a>
                           began, fueled by rumors that they were encouraging
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miscegenation" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Miscegenation">
                            miscegenation
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1915" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1915">
                            1915
                           </a>
                           
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinhalese_people" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Sinhalese people">
                            Sinhalese
                           </a>
                           army officer
                           <b>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Pedris" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Henry Pedris">
                             Henry Pedris
                            </a>
                           </b>
                           was wrongly executed by
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Ceylon" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="British Ceylon">
                            British authorities
                           </a>
                           for allegedly inciting race riots, hastening the
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lankan_independence_movement" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Sri Lankan independence movement">
                            Sri Lankan independence movement
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1994">
                            1994
                           </a>
                            Troops from the former
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemen_Arab_Republic" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Yemen Arab Republic">
                            North Yemen
                           </a>
                           captured
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aden" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Aden">
                            Aden
                           </a>
                           , ending the
                           <b>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yemeni_Civil_War_(1994)" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Yemeni Civil War (1994)">
                             Yemeni civil war
                            </a>
                           </b>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="2005">
                            2005
                           </a>
                            Suicide bombers
                           <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casualties_of_the_7_July_2005_London_bombings" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Casualties of the 7 July 2005 London bombings">
                            killed 52 people
                           </a>
                           in
                           <b>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">
                             a series of four explosions
                            </a>
                           </b>
                           on
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transport_in_London" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Transport in London">
                            London's public transport system
                           </a>
                           <i>
                            (emergency responders pictured)
                           </i>
                           .
                          </li>
                         </ul>
                        </div>
                        <div>
                         <span style="color: red; font-family: Helvetica Neue, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                          <span style="background-color: white; line-height: 18px;">
                           It is good to be innocent, but bad to be executed if you are innocent. Don't riot against abolitionists, but argue with them, and prove, through logic, you are the master race. Now Henry, we've covered this and you should accept it. It is good the civil war is over. London deserved better, but she endures. Let's party.
                          </span>
                         </span>
                        </div>

                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1124" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1124">
                            1124
                           </a>
                           
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Tyre, Lebanon">
                            Tyre
                           </a>
                           falls to the
                           <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusaders" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Crusaders">

                           .

                            1456
                           </a>
                            A
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrial_of_Joan_of_Arc" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Retrial of Joan of Arc">
                            retrial verdict
                           </a>
                           acquits
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Joan of Arc">
                            Joan of Arc
                           </a>
                           of
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heresy_in_Christianity" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Heresy in Christianity">
                            heresy
                           </a>
                           25 years after her death.
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1520" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1520">
                            1520
                           </a>
                            Spanish
                           <i>
                            <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquistador" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Conquistador">
                             conquistadores
                            </a>
                           </i>
                           defeat a larger
                           <a class="mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aztec_Triple_Alliance" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Aztec Triple Alliance">
                            Aztec
                           </a>
                           army at the
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Otumba" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Battle of Otumba">
                            Battle of Otumba
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1534" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1534">
                            1534
                           </a>
                           
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="European colonization of the Americas">
                            European colonization of the Americas
                           </a>
                           : First known exchange between Europeans and natives of the
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">
                            Gulf of St. Lawrence
                           </a>
                           in
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Brunswick" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="New Brunswick">
                            New Brunswick
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1543" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1543">
                            1543
                           </a>
                            French troops invade
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Luxembourg">
                            Luxembourg
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1575" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="1575">
                            1575
                           </a>
                           
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raid_of_the_Redeswire" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Raid of the Redeswire">
                            Raid of the Redeswire
                           </a>
                           , the last major battle between
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Kingdom of England">
                            England
                           </a>
                           and
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Kingdom of Scotland">
                            Scotland
                           </a>
                           .
                          </li>
                          <li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;">

                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestantism" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Protestantism">

                           in France.

                           </a>

                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-War" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Quasi-War">

                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Underwood" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Peter Underwood">
                            Peter Underwood
                           </a>
                           , Australian lawyer and politician, 27th
                           <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_Tasmania" style="background-image: none; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial; color: #0b0080; text-decoration: none;" title="Governor of Tasmania">
                            Governor of Tasmania
                           </a>
                           (b. 1937)
                          </li>
                         </ul>

                Bill Shorten
                <a href="http://www.abc.net.au/news/2015-07-07/bill-shorten-outlines-dreams-for-australia-in-pub-speech/6600794" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">

               </div>

                 </i>

                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  In the video obtained by the ABC, rowdy Labor supporters cheer as an emotional Mr Shorten tells the crowd he dreams of an Australia where same-sex marriage is legalised, Indigenous people are recognised in the constitution, and where people can organise to have a strong minimum wage and

                   they will not be subject to a royal commission
                  </b>
                  .

              <h3 style="background-attachment: scroll; background-color: #eeecdd; background-image: url(http://resources.news.com.au/cs/network/images/third-party/blogs/images/blogassets/images_core/v2/bkg_posttitle.gif); background-position: 100% 0%; background-repeat: no-repeat no-repeat; box-sizing: content-box; clear: none; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; margin: 2px 0px 0px; padding: 0.2em 2.5em 0.2em 0.5em; position: relative;">
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/dailytelegraph/timblair/index.php/dailytelegraph/comments/decision_first_audit_second/" rel="bookmark" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; text-decoration: none;">
                DECISION FIRST, AUDIT SECOND
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="border-bottom-color: rgb(207, 207, 209); border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1px; box-sizing: content-box; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 0.95em; margin: 0.7em 8px 1em; padding: 0px 0px 0.2em;">
               Tim Blair
               <span class="datestamp" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #616b77; font-size: inherit; font-style: italic; font-weight: normal;">
                <span class="dash" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 
                </span>
                <span class="dayname" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 Tuesday
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  ,
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="month" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 07
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  ,
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="year" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  (
                 </span>
                 11:23am
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  )
                 </span>
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary" style="box-sizing: content-box; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; margin: 2px 8px;">
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                ABC-appointed
                <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 Q &amp; A
                </i>
                auditor Ray Martins
                <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/federal-politics/political-news/qa-auditor-ray-martin-derides-tony-abbotts-silly-frontbench-boycott-20150707-gi6lal" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">
                 completely unbiased and independent view
                </a>
                :
               </div>
               <blockquote style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  The man chosen to conduct an independent audit of Q&amp;A, television veteran Ray Martin, says he cannot believe Prime Minister Tony Abbott has ordered his frontbenchers not to appear on the ABC program until his inquiry is complete.
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  As well as decrying the governments Q&amp;A boycott as silly, Martin said he believes Q&amp;A host Tony Jones was as tough on the previous Labor government as the Coalition.
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  Mr Martin said some of the rants and raves about the program had been crazy and that he hoped his audit would
                  <b style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                   bring some balance to the debate
                  </b>
                  
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  The program has up to one million viewers a week and provides a good forum for politicians to sell their message, Martin said.
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  I cant imagine Australia without the ABC so Ive got a lot of time [for it] but that doesnt mean that it cant be better, he said 
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  Following Mr Martins comments, an ABC spokesman said he was chosen to conduct the audit because he is independent and the public perceive him to be.
                 </i>
                </div>
               </blockquote>
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                The second part of that final comment is much more important than the first. As for Martins line about bringing some balance to the debate, how can that possibly be the role of an audit?
               </div>
              </div>

                <a href="https://www.google.com.au/search?q=%22which+was+reimbursed+by+The+NZ+Initiative%22&amp;oq=%22which+was+reimbursed+by+The+NZ+Initiative%22&amp;aqs=chrome..69i57.6735j0j4&amp;sourceid=chrome&amp;es_sm=122&amp;ie=UTF-8#safe=off&amp;q=AGD_AE15-103" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/turnbull_cool_on_the_abbott_war_talk/" rel="bookmark">
                Turnbull cool on the Abbott war talk
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (7:57pm)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <h3 style="background-attachment: scroll; background-color: #eeecdd; background-image: url(http://resources.news.com.au/cs/network/images/third-party/blogs/images/blogassets/images_core/v2/bkg_posttitle.gif); background-position: 100% 0%; background-repeat: no-repeat no-repeat; box-sizing: content-box; clear: none; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 1.4em; margin: 2px 0px 0px; padding: 0.2em 2.5em 0.2em 0.5em; position: relative;">
               <div class="post-categories">
               </div>
               <div class="postsummary">
                Politically not a useful contribution, but
                <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/federal-politics/political-news/dont-overestimate-islamic-state-threat-malcolm-turnbull-20150707-gi7715.html" title=" Malcolm Turnbull is telling the truth:">
                 Malcolm Turnbull is telling the truth:
                </a>
                <br/>
                <blockquote>
                 <em>
                  The threat posed by the Islamic State terror
 group should not be overstated, and critics of new national security 
measures should not be denounced, Communications Minister Malcolm 
Turnbull has said.
                 </em>
                 <br/>
                 <em>
                  In a speech that strikes a jarringly different tone from recent remarks 
by Prime Minister Tony Abbott, Mr Turnbull said on Tuesday evening that 
making tough national security polices might be popular but can still
 be a mistake.
                  <br/>
                  He used a Sydney Institute address to call for respectful, open debate 
on national security in which new measures could be questioned without 
inviting opprobrium.
                  <br/>
                  Just as it is important not to underestimate, or be complacent about, 
the national security threat from Daesh, it is equally important not to 
overestimate that threat, he said, using an alternative name for 
Islamic State.
                  <br/>
                 </em>
                 <em>
                  He said Islamic State was not Hitlers Germany, Tojos Japan or 
Stalins Russia and despite the terror groups own aspirations to world
 domination, we should be careful not to say or do things which can be 
seen to add credibility to those delusions.
                 </em>
                </blockquote>
                I fear the Abbott Government is getting diminishing returns from its 
anti-terrorism agenda, which in time might be seen to be cover for a 
lack of other policies.
                <br/>
                But here I think Turnbull is too dismissive:
                <br/>
                <blockquote>
                 <em>
                  I suppose there is nothing tougher than 
invading a country, overthrowing its government and occupying its 
territory. But with the benefit of hindsight, few today contend that the
 2003 invasion of Iraq, popular with the US public and the Congress at 
the time, was not a tragic error.
                  <br/>
                 </em>
                </blockquote>
                There is no doubt from the weapons inspectors reports that Saddam was 
ready to resume his programs for weapons of mass destruction once the 
pressure went off. Imagine the Middle East with those now in terrorist 
hands. Imagine also the Middle East with Saddam or his mad sons left 
unchecked. Imagine Libya with the nuclear weapons program that Gaddafi 
in fear surrendered after the Iraq war.
                <br/>
                In all this we are speculating on hypotheticals, of course. But it is as well to be modest in predicting the costs of inaction.
                <br/>
                UPDATE
                <br/>
                Turnbull may still be feeling his oats. The Government is still behind 
in the polls, and Australias biggest media organisation is looking for a
 hero to save them from that wicked Abbott:
                <br/>
                <blockquote>
                 <em>
                  Communications Minister
                  <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/business/media/qa-tony-abbotts-ministerial-boycott-silly-says-ray-martin/story-fna045gd-1227431970724" title="Malcolm Turnbull has not ruled out appearing on the next edition of the ABC's controversial Q&amp;A program">
                   Malcolm Turnbull has not ruled out appearing on the next edition of the ABCs controversial Q&amp;A program
                  </a>
                  .
                 </em>
                 <br/>
                 <em>
                  Despite a ban on coalition MPs from appearing on the show, the minister says it will depend on the circumstances.
                  <br/>
                 </em>
                 <em>
                  Time will tell - stay tuned, he told reporters in Sydney tonight.
                 </em>
                </blockquote>
               </div>
              </h3>
