              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/union_official_charged/" rel="bookmark">
                Union official charged
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (4:48pm)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               Brennan must be considered innocent until and unless proved guilty:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 <a href="http://www.abc.net.au/news/2015-07-07/stephen-brennan-ex-union-official-facing-dishonesty-charges/6601168" title="Prosecutors expect to lay 10 more charges against a former South Australian and Tasmanian union official who is accused of dishonesty">
                  Prosecutors
 expect to lay 10 more charges against a former South Australian and 
Tasmanian union official who is accused of dishonesty
                 </a>
                 , a court has been told.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 Stephen Brennan, 49, is facing 22 charges of falsifying accounts and 28 of dishonestly dealing with documents.
                 <br/>
                 It is alleged Brennan committed the offences while he was secretary of 
the South Australian and Tasmanian branch of the Textile, Clothing and 
Footwear Union
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 Brennan had moved to the job of employee ombudsman in SA when the 
union-related allegations arose. He took leave from that job in 2013, on
 full pay of about $143,000 annually, until the office was abolished 
this year. A government official said Brennan was no longer on the 
public payroll.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               I repeat, these are just allegations and Brennan must be presumed 
innocent. But the line about just a few rotten apples in the union 
movement is starting to wear extremely thin after all allegations about 
the AWU, CFMEU, Health Services Union and more.
              </div>

                Cheers, Bill
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">

                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="200" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/khNldHLs0xI?feature=player_embedded" width="350">
               </iframe>
               There is one thing about
               <a href="http://mobile.abc.net.au/news/2015-07-07/bill-shorten-outlines-dreams-for-australia-in-pub-speech/6600794" title=" Bill Shorten's shouting performance in the pub ">
                Bill Shortens shouting performance in the pub
               </a>
               that the ABC reporter seems too polite to mention:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 A day before his highly anticipated appearance before
 the Royal Commission into Trade Union Governance and Corruption, video 
has emerged of Opposition Leader Bill Shorten passionately outlining his
 vision for Australia inside a Sydney pub.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 In the video obtained by the ABC, rowdy Labor supporters cheer as an 
emotional Mr Shorten tells the crowd he dreams of an Australia where 
same-sex marriage is legalised, Indigenous people are recognised in the 
constitution, and where people can organise to have a strong minimum 
wage and they will not be subject to a royal commission.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 The video was filmed in Sydneys Covent Garden pub on Sunday night.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               The yelling about the royal commission seems particularly heartfelt.
               <br/>
               UPDATE
               <br/>
               If Abbott shouted in public in that kind of emotional state, would the ABC have covered it with this nonchalance?
               <br/>
               (Thanks to reader Duncan.)

              <br/>
              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/costello_greece_is_a_warning/" rel="bookmark">
                Costello: Greece is a warning
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (11:09am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               Greece, in a bizarre 
display of Leftist machismo,  is demanding Europe give it even more 
money it will never repay - and without asking the Greeks to at least 
make some reforms to its handout economy.
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.heraldsun.com.au/news/opinion/forget-the-rhetoric-greece-has-no-control/story-fni0ffsx-1227431254721" title="Former Treasurer Peter Costello:">
                Former Treasurer Peter Costello:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <em>
               </em>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Greece has run out of money. The Government cant pay back its debt  it
 cant make the full interest payments on its debt. The banks cant pay 
their depositors. Thats why they are closed except to allow depositors 
to withdraw 60 euros a day.
                 <br/>
                 No one wants to lend more money to the Greek Government and the Greek 
banks. For the sake of preventing fallout from the Greek crisis 
spreading through Europe, the Europeans and the IMF came up with a new 
lending proposal on June 25. It included some pretty strict terms. 
Greece has just rejected them.
                 <br/>
                 If Greece were in control of its destiny, the Government would now get 
on with its own policy ideas. It would fund them by borrowing and 
issuing Greek bonds to investors. But no one will buy them.
                 <br/>
                 So Tsipras will get off to Brussels at the first available opportunity 
to seek new terms on a proposed loan package. Greek destiny will be 
decided in Brussels
                 <br/>
                 If the Greeks were really concerned about their sovereignty and destiny, the time to have shown it was long before now.
                 <br/>
                 All through the 1990s and 2000s Greece was paying people pensions that 
it couldnt afford. It awarded itself pay rises that couldnt be 
justified. Tax rates were well below the level that was required to pay 
for all that spending. And thats if they were actually being paid as 
opposed to routinely avoided.
                 <br/>
                 The whole country was living high on the hog and doing it by borrowing 
(and spending) other peoples money. That works quite well right up 
until the point that other people dont want to lend you any more. 
Thats when you have lost control of your destiny.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 <br/>
                 There is a lesson here for other countries. The time to worry about debt
 is before it gets out of control. The Australian Government is still 
borrowing $100 million a day.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Which makes the idiocy of Greens Senator Larissa Waters even more risible - despite the fact it was applauded by last nights
               <em>
                Q&amp;A
               </em>
               audience: You cant cut your way to prosperity.
               <br/>
               Actually, you cant overspend your way to prosperity, which is exactly 
what Greece has tried and what the Greens would try, too, if we were mad
 enough to vote them in.
              </div>
              ===

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/ray_martin_proves_the_abc_is_trying_to_con_us/" rel="bookmark">
                Ray Martin proves the ABC is trying to con us
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (10:59am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               I warned on
               <em>
                The Bolt Report
               </em>
               that the ABC inquiry into
               <em>
                Q&amp;A
               </em>
               was
               <a href="http://www.heraldsun.com.au/video/id-tsZG4xdjpnYw8DJ4HaEnUJoCiJRJ4wLb/NEWSWATCH" title=" a typical ABC stitch-up">
                a typical ABC stitch-up
               </a>
               . I mean, appointing Ray Martin to check the ABC for Left-wing bias? Seriously?
               <br/>
               And just days later the farce is exposed:
               <br/>
               <em>
               </em>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Television journalist
                 <a href="http://www.google.com.au/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=1&amp;cad=rja&amp;uact=8&amp;ved=0CCkQFjAA&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.theaustralian.com.au%2Fbusiness%2Fmedia%2Fqa-tony-abbotts-ministerial-boycott-silly-says-ray-martin%2Fstory-fna045gd-1227431970724&amp;ei=7CSbVa2nHYiF8QWQoLyYDA&amp;usg=AFQjCNG7Oh14S5c5KmIkK_15AVSJAE2ayA&amp;bvm=bv.96952980,d.dGc" title="Ray Martin has appeared to prejudge the inquiry he is yet to conduct into Q&amp;A">
                  Ray Martin has appeared to prejudge the inquiry he is yet to conduct into Q&amp;A
                 </a>
                 by saying he thinks the rants and raves about the program have been a little crazy.
                 <br/>
                 <br/>
                 On Channel Seven this morning, Martin defended both the ABC and Q&amp;A 
host Tony Jones when Sunrise host Samantha Armytage asked him about the 
upcoming review.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 He said everyone needs a Bex and a good lie down and described Tony Abbotts boycott of the program as silly.
                 <br/>
                 I thought it was about time for a little balance. I thought the rants 
and raves were a little crazy about that thing so it was time to at 
least have a look at what it was about, Martin said.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 I cant imagine Australia without the ABC so Ive got a lot of time but
 that doesnt mean that it cant be better. But I tended to think ... I 
cant believe, its clearly a political issue at the moment in terms of 
terror. I think weve already started looking towards the next 
election.
                 <br/>
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               The ABC has tried to snow us again in the typical ABC way, in which 
everyone agrees with each other that conservatives are wrong.
               <br/>
               Abbotts boycott suddenly looks more justifiable.
               <br/>
               UPDATE
               <br/>
               <a href="http://mumbrella.com.au/ray-martin-abc-qa-review-as-program-broadcast-303087" title="Malcolm Turnbull's statement welcoming the ABC's selection of  Martin  ">
                Malcolm Turnbulls statement welcoming the ABCs selection of  Martin
               </a>
               was far too generous and far too nave:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 I welcome their associated decision to initiate an 
independent review of Q&amp;A to be undertaken by the former Managing 
Director of SBS, Mr Shaun Brown and the distinguished television 
journalist, Mr Ray Martin.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Martin now declares his findings before hes held his inquiry:
               <br/>
               <em>
               </em>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 SAMANTHA ARMYTAGE: ... you are currently conducting an audit of the ABCs Q&amp;A programme.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 RAY MARTIN: I am, with a former boss of SBS. I thought it was about time
 for a little balance. The rants and raves were a bit crazy about thing 
so it was at least time to have a look at what it was about. I have a 
lot of time, but I cant imagine Australia without the ABC, so Ive got a
 lot of time. That doesnt mean they cant be better but I tended to 
think it was  I cant believe  its clearly a political issue at the 
moment in terms of terror. I think weve already started looking towards
 the next election.
                 <br/>
                 SAMANTHA ARMYTAGE: Are you allowed to say where you sit exactly on  
whats his name, Zaky Mallah, appearing on the show that Monday night?
                 <br/>
                 RAY MARTIN: I think everyone agrees it was a mistake to have him live  
no question about that. They had Hicks on pre-recorded. It was a mistake
 to have him there. But the rest, Im sort of going to wait and see. 
Were looking back at the last 22 programmes. I would like to see what 
happened last year, as well  the year before, rather, when there was a 
Labor Government. I suspect Tony Jones was just as tough on the Labor 
Government as he has been on the Coalition right now. But I think, you 
know, a Bex and a good lie down might help at the moment.
                 <br/>
                 SAMANTHA ARMYTAGE: What do you make of Abbott banning his frontbenchers from appearing?
                 <br/>
                 RAY MARTIN: I cant believe it. I just think it is so silly to do it. I 
would have thought that Barnaby Joyce, who wasnt on last night, should 
have said, Look, Im not a member of the Liberal Party, Im a member of
 the National Party, and I can do what I like, and go and do it. And 
what Malcolm Turnbull does next week, he is booked for next week  I 
suspect that he would still like the top job and I suspect he wont come
 but I think its silly
                 <br/>
                 SAMANTHA ARMYTAGE: Do you think this is just a thing where the Liberal 
Government will ban it for a while and then it will sort of move on  
everyone will forget.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 RAY MARTIN: You would think they would have to. It is, as someone said 
last night, close to a million people watch that programme on a Monday 
night and a politician giving up access to that. When you think of 
Malcolm Turnbull and Christopher Pyne, they seem to be there every 
second week, so its a great forum for people to talk and I would have 
thought the questions there  and I notice the ABC is now running a 
promo that says something like where your questions count or something
 like that.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Whats the point of the review if Martin has made up his mind already? Or is this exactly why the ABC chose him?
               <br/>
               What a farce.
              </div>

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/churches_beware_the_same_sex_marriage_push_is_a_trojan_horse/" rel="bookmark">
                Churches beware: the same-sex marriage push is a Trojan Horse
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (10:18am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               Some in the same-sex marriage push are not into tolerance at all, and
               <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/gay-marriage-church-could-opt-out-of-legal-weddings/story-fn59niix-1227431436010" title=" churches have every right to worry about this new war on their faith">
                churches have every right to worry about this new war on their faith
               </a>
               :
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Tasmanian gay rights activist Martine Delaney  who 
yesterday confirmed she would run as a Greens candidate for the federal 
seat of Franklin  pursues a legal claim against the Catholic Church 
over a pastoral letter explaining its opposition to the redefinition of
 marriage Ms Delaney told WIN News at the weekend she was taking her 
complaint about the Catholic pamphlet, titled Dont Mess with Marriage, 
to the states anti-discrimination commissioner.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               So this work is urgent and important:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Liberal Democrat senator David Leyonhjelm ... slammed Labors marriage 
equality bill for falling short on the protection of religious freedoms.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 Following a key meeting last week, the NSW Presbyterian Assembly 
proposed its ministers be prohibited from conducting legal marriages if 
the law was changed. The assembly considered what the church should do 
if marriage is redefined in Australia. It decided to ask the General 
Assembly of Australia to withdraw the whole church from the Marriage 
Act, so that our ministers could no longer solemnise marriages under the
 Marriage Act, said a July 3 pastoral letter.
                 <br/>
                 NSW [Presbyterian Assembly]  moderator Kevin Murray told The Australian
 the church was concerned about exposure to possible discrimination 
action
                 <br/>
                 [Freedom commissioner Tim] Wilson has proposed civil and religious 
traditions of marriage be separated yet treated equally at law, while 
wedding service providers could also choose to restrict their business 
to traditional weddings.
                 <br/>
                 The Anglican Bishop of South Sydney, Robert Forsyth, welcomed Mr 
Wilsons contribution for addressing the effect of gay marriage on 
religious freedom.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 Senator Leyonhjelms 2014 freedom to marry bill seeks to mollify 
conservatives by allowing civil celebrants to refuse to marry homosexual
 couples on conscience grounds, a point he says Labor and the Greens 
overlook.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               No, the Left does not overlook this at all. Too many of their members 
are just intellectual thugs, seeking to impose their views by force.
               <br/>
               (Thanks to reader WaG311.)

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/the_abc_is_out_of_control/" rel="bookmark">
                The ABC is out of control
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (9:58am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/opinion/peppa-pig-or-politics-what-is-the-abc-for/story-e6frg6zo-1227431213860" title="Nick Cater says the ABC has become an autonomous soviet ">
                Nick Cater says the ABC has become an autonomous soviet
               </a>
               beyond the power of any government to make   accountable and fair:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 The governments prerogative to overrule the ABCs editorial decisions 
was removed from legislation in 1983. Since then, the ABC effectively 
has become a foreign country, outside the jurisdiction of the 
Commonwealth of Australia, save for the approval of its sizeable 
stipend. It enjoys power without responsibility which, as British 
Conservative politician Stanley Baldwin once remarked, was the 
prerogative of the harlot throughout the ages.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 So what, if anything, can a level-headed government do to ensure its 
annual billion-dollar investment is well spent? Should it try to wrest 
control of the state-owned station from the barmy bohemians who occupy 
it? Or should it just boycott their shows?
                 <br/>
                 Would the appointment of a managing director with spine prevent, for 
example, the bussing of terrorist sympathisers from Parramatta to 
broadcast live to the nation? Not a hope if history is any guide. 
Malcolm Fraser went to war with the ABC in his first year of government 
but had run up the white flag by Christmas.
                 <br/>
                 Bob Hawke settled for an uneasy truce. John Howard stacked the board 
with decent chaps who found themselves powerless to influence the 
corporation in any significant way whatsoever.
                 <br/>
                 The iron law of culturally autonomous government-funded bodies is that they are far easier to set up than to close down.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               <a href="http://catallaxyfiles.com/2015/07/06/if-only-the-taxpayer-could-boycott-the-abc-too/">
                Sinclair Davidson:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <i>
                 The ABC suffers from a profound governance problem  the controlling 
shareholder (i.e. federal government) exercises no oversight into the 
ABCs activities. The ABC has the trappings of control  a board that 
seems to exercise zero control over the organisation. The controlling 
shareholder is so disengaged that it no longer appoints people to the 
board, rather it appoints the people who appoint the people. Really? 
That is how the government thinks over $1 billion of taxpayer funds 
should be administered?
                </i>
                <br/>
                <i>
                 Then there is the issue of the ABC charter embedded in the ABC Act. It 
is widely accepted that the ABC does not comply with the charter. Why 
should it? The charter is not self-enforcing. The ABC Act contains no 
mechanism to monitor compliance with the charter and to punish deviation
 from the charter. The Board is powerless to do so and the government 
unwilling to do so. It is not simply a case of when the cats away the 
mice will play  there are no cats. The ABC is not out of control, the 
ABC has no control.
                 <br/>
                 So for Abbott and his front bench to boycott the ABC is very lazy 
policy and simply of continuance of the hands off policy that has 
allowed the ABC to degenerate to its current form. A far more sensible 
policy would be exert control over the organisation and insert 
enforcement mechanism into the charter.
                 <br/>
                </i>
                <i>
                 Of course, the counter-argument is that government shouldnt control the
 media. I agree  but then the government shouldnt own the media 
either.
                </i>
               </blockquote>
               <a href="http://www.canberratimes.com.au/comment/coalition-boycott-of-abcs-qa-program-long-overdue-20150706-gi60jg.html">
                Patrick Hannaford:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <i>
                 Abbotts decision has provoked outrage from political opponents. Some even suggested that its an attack on freedom of speech.
                </i>
                <br/>
                <i>
                 But no one would suggest Abbott was attacking freedom of speech by 
declining an interview with Green-Left Weekly. The political bias of the
 publication is clear for all to see
                 <br/>
                 Unfortunately, this is an accurate comparison. Despite its attempts at 
objectivity, the institutional make-up of the ABC is clear.
                 <br/>
                 In a 2013 survey of Australian journalists, 41 per cent of ABC staff 
declared the Greens most closely reflected their political attitudes ...
 A further 32 per cent of ABC journalists surveyed declared they would 
give their first preference to the ALP.
                 <br/>
                 With these demographics, it is remarkable the ABCs current affairs team
 has remained as objective as it has. Unfortunately Q&A;has not met 
this same standard
                 <br/>
                </i>
                <i>
                 Q&amp;A is a show that favours demagoguery and gotcha journalism. A 
hostile environment for any government interested in serious policy 
discussion. And Tony Abbott is right to declare a boycott.
                </i>
               </blockquote>
               (Thanks to reader Peter of Bellevue Hill.)

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/pearson_contradicts_pearson_no_treating_aborigines_as_a_separate_race_is_il/" rel="bookmark">
                Pearson contradicts Pearson: no, treating Aborigines as a separate race  is illegitimate
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (9:28am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="post-categories">
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/C997/">
                Culture wars
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/C993/">
                The politics of race
               </a>
              </div>
              <br/>
              <div class="postsummary">
               Is Aboriginal leader 
Noel Pearson hopelessly confused about the society he wants to build 
with his plan for an Aborigines-only Parliament or advisory body in the 
Constitution?
               <br/>
               Pearson on
               <em>
                Lateline
               </em>
               last night
               <a href="http://www.abc.net.au/lateline/content/2015/s4268680.htm" title="contradicted himself last night in a very significant way">
                contradicted himself last night in a very significant way
               </a>
               .
               <br/>
               First Pearson said yes to race"-based politics - to people being represented not as citizens but members of a race:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 NOEL PEARSON: The question should be about including Indigenous people 
in the democratic process of this country, to include them as 
participants in our robust democratic debate and policy development and 
law development.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 EMMA ALBERICI: Arent they already there, and pardon my naivety, we have Ken Wyatt, we have Nova Peris.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 NOEL PEARSON: ... But at the end of the day, if I ever had chosen a 
political path, youd represent your seat. Thats your duty as an 
Australian politician. Ken has the people of Hasluck as his first 
concern and Nova has the people of the Northern Territory, black and 
white, as her constituents. And any Indigenous person or Greek or 
Italian person in Parliament they - of course they bring their own 
ethnic priorities to the table, but at the starting point, they are 
representatives of a seat. The question were concerned about is this 
whole thing of Indigenous peoples representation on Indigenous issues 
and thats why Ive been pushing the idea of a constitutional body that 
would enable us as Indigenous people to talk about our heritage, our 
communities, our native title and our languages and culture in a way 
that Parliament can hear us. So, I continue to make that argument that 
recognition must involve that.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               But then Pearson said  no to race"-based politics - to treating each other as members of a race:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 NOEL PEARSON: Um, yeah - well at the moment, for example, were 
characterised as a race. Thats what the Constitution characterises us, 
and it infects our whole psychology, not just the black fellas, the 
white fellas too, cause the white fellas think were a separate race 
and treat us as a race, an illegitimate idea, and we ourselves have 
internalised that.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               This occurred in the same interview. Pearson, I believe, in his heart 
now knows that all hes been agitating for is actually a sin against our
 common humanity. A sin again the teachings of Christ, part of his 
Lutheran upbringing, and
               <a href="http://www.google.com.au/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=video&amp;cd=1&amp;cad=rja&amp;uact=8&amp;ved=0CBwQtwIwAA&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3Dvx3Z8ZToq3c&amp;ei=dhGbVcC8BZGE8gWA_quYBw&amp;usg=AFQjCNE3ExyMWvjtnJ4uaIy9fi5XCr2kBg&amp;bvm=bv.96952980,d.dGc" title="against the preaching ">
                against the preaching
               </a>
               of Martin Luther King, one of his heroes.
               <br/>
               Lets just agree that dividing people by race is vile, and end this whole push now, before even more damage is done.
               <br/>
               UPDATE
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/in-depth/call-for-a-treaty-spanner-in-the-works-of-recognition-bid/story-fnihym2m-1227431204818">
                Anthony Dillon:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 At least two Aboriginal leaders have suggested the need for treaties between Australia and Aboriginal nations
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 What exactly can a treaty achieve for Aboriginal people today that 
cannot already be achieved without it? How does a treaty relate to 
constitutional recognition? ...
                 <br/>
                 Despite calls for a treaty, many Aborigines, several thousand in fact, are doing exceedingly well without one....
                 <br/>
                 But if a treaty is to be pursued, it cannot be discussed without discussing the elephant in the room  who is an Aborigine?
                 <br/>
                 What happens in the case of someone like myself  a part-Aboriginal 
Australian who has both Aboriginal and non-Aboriginal ancestry? Will a 
treaty highlight differences between those Australians with Aboriginal 
ancestry and those with no Aboriginal ancestry and potentially polarise 
the two groups?
                 <br/>
                 I fear that chasing a treaty will remove the unity from community, when 
we should be thinking of all Australians as belonging to one community. 
Experience has shown that once indigenous identity is open for 
discussion, claims of offence are sure to follow.
                 <br/>
                 Finally, my concern is that chasing a treaty will be another great 
distraction from addressing the problems we know need to be addressed, 
but that few wish to acknowledge, such as violence, child abuse, and 
drug and alcohol abuse, all of which are killing Aborigines; yet many 
are happy to sit by and chase the next fad.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Of course, some of the critical issues raised by Dillon are now too 
legally dangerous to frankly discuss, and this push will, if successful,
 make even more important topics legally off-limits.
               <br/>
               (Thanks to reader WaG311.)
              </div>

               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/abbott_weakens_qa_abc_abuses_its_power_by_hitting_back/" rel="bookmark">

               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>

              <div class="postsummary">
               <em>

               </em>
               was 
quite boring last night  without a Coalition MP on - a bit like the 
Christian not turning up to the colosseum to meet the lions -  and the 
ABC should be alarmed.
               <br/>

Left have been thrown into attacking the Government, in yet another 
demonstration of the ABCs reflexively Leftist groupthink. Heres
               <a href="http://www.abc.net.au/7.30/content/2015/s4268627.htm" title=" Leigh Sales badgering a Liberal frontbencher on 7.30">

                </em>

 to speak to 900,000 voters every week. You want to give that up?

scream his last to 90,000 hooting spectators. Does he really want to 
give that up?

               <em>
                Q&amp;A
               </em>
               last night:
               <br/>

               </em>

                 </a>
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               <em>
               </em>
               Gosh, people on
               <em>
                Q&amp;A
               </em>
               criticising those who wont go on? What a surprise.
               <br/>
               <blockquote>

convicted criminal and known extremist Zaky Mallah last month used the

 Marles used the program to say Mr Abbotts boycott was an attempt to

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/so_far_that_predicted_heat_sure_isnt_here/" rel="bookmark">
                So far that predicted heat sure isnt here
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (8:23am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               Once again we must ask: are the Bureau of Meteorologys climate models tuned to run too hot? Too alarmist?
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/environment/weather/bureau-of-meteorology-declares-el-nino-event-in-australia-20150512-ggzdgy.html" title="alarmist Peter Hannam on 12 May:">
                <em>
                 Sydney Morning Herald
                </em>
                paid alarmist Peter Hannam on 12 May:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 A substantial El Nino event has begun, raising the likelihood of 
worsening drought over inland Australia and higher daytime temperatures,
 the Bureau of Meteorology said
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 Relatively clear skies mean daytime temperatures across much of the 
country tend to be above average Australias temperatures are about one
 degree above average in the second half of the calendar year during El 
Nino events, adding to the background warming signal from climate 
change, Dr Jones said.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/environment/weather/weeks-of-chill-ahead-as-polar-air-moves-in-over-australia-20150706-gi5xw1.html" title="Peter Hannam today:">
                Peter Hannam today:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <em>
               </em>
               <em>
               </em>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Sydneys run of exceptionally chilly mornings 
could become the citys coldest spell in more than three decades  and a
 return to milder conditions may be weeks away....
                 <br/>
                 The citys below-average temperatures, in other words, may be more 
likely during the day than at night. It will start to affect day-time 
temperatures more than night-time temperatures because [next weeks 
front] looks like its probably got a lot of cloud and moisture attached
 to it, Mr Dutschke said.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               True, weve still got that second half of the year to go, but so far so cold.
               <br/>
               (Thanks to reader Dazza.)

              <br/>
              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/why_are_aboriginal_leaders_debating_words_and_not_murders/" rel="bookmark">
                Why are Aboriginal leaders debating words and not murders?
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (8:01am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               How he reconciliation movement is in fact doing the very opposite - driving Australians into opposing racial camps:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Cape York leader
                 <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/indigenous/plebiscite-plan-flows-from-historic-summit/story-fn9hm1pm-1227431483163" title="Noel Pearson has called for an Aboriginal plebiscite on constitutional recognition ">
                  Noel Pearson has called for an Aboriginal plebiscite on constitutional recognition
                 </a>
                 to be held ahead of a referendum, in a bid to secure an overwhelming display of indigenous unity on the issue.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Who gets to vote in this plebiscite? Will one Aboriginal 
great-great-grandparent in your ancestry qualify you as an Aborigine, 
with different rights? Why such absurd one drop rules? What madness is
 this? And what a criminal distraction from the real and grave problems 
on the ground, like this - which none of the 40 Aboriginal leaders who
 met yesterday with the Prime Minister are today discussing:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 ... the Northern Territory [is] ... the homicide capital of Australia. 
Statistics from the Australian Institute of Criminology show
                 <a href="http://www.news.com.au/national/crime/the-northern-territory-has-the-highest-homicide-rate-in-australia/story-fns0kb1g-1227431505075" title="the homicide rate for the NT was 5.5 per 100,000 people. This is five times the national rate">
                  the homicide rate for the NT was 5.5 per 100,000 people. This is five times the national rate
                 </a>
                 and almost four times the second highest state, Western Australia, which had a homicide rate of 1.4 per 100,000
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 In 2001-02, the NTs rate was almost six times higher than the national 
average, 11.5 compared to 1.9. By 2011-12 it had improved significantly 
to 5.5, but was still higher than the rest of the country
                 <br/>
                 So why does the Top End have a higher rate?
                 <br/>
                 Its a combination of factors, [Matthew Willis, research officer from 
the AIC] said But there are also higher levels of violence and, in 
particular, the higher rate of alcohol-related violence particularly in 
indigenous communities in the NT.
                 <br/>
                  And the rates of family violence among indigenous people is much higher than non-indigenous...
                 <br/>
                 Mr Willis said in recent years there appeared to be higher concentration
 of homicides in the Alice Springs area. He attributed this to the 
region being a central point for outer-lying communities.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 When you end up with people from different communities coming together 
 you get those sort of tensions and issues that come with people being 
crowded together, especially when they are in situations where they are 
drinking, he added.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Frightening levels of murder, domestic violence and drinking in 
Aboriginal communities, and our top Aboriginal leaders are spending 
their time talking instead about changing words in the constitution? 
Seriously?
               <br/>
               UPDATE
               <br/>
               The fact is that the leaders of the reconciliation movement are 
unappeasable. Should they ever admit we are indeed reconciled they will 
lose their self-righteous anger, their power and their funding - their 
whole shtick. And so even now, the day after the top 40 Aboriginal 
leaders get a big meeting with the Prime Minister and Opposition Leader,
 both saying they are committed to delivering what the reconcilers 
want, we get this:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Noel Pearson has blasted the Prime Minister and Opposition Leader 
after a summit on Indigenous recognition in Sydney, saying while the 
event was a good start, it was stage-managed and left a bitter 
taste in his mouth
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 As the founder of the Cape York Institute for Policy and Leadership and a
 prominent Indigenous leader, Mr Pearson ... [said] he would have 
preferred to stay in Cape York ... and sent a cardboard cut-out to the
 meeting instead.
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 I had a grin across my face for most of the morning but ... having been
 manoeuvred through the morning towards a pre-determined outcome started
 to taste a bit bitter in my mouth.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               Does this sound like reconciliation to you?
              </div>
              ===
              <br/>
              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/matters_for_shorten_to_explain/" rel="bookmark">
                Matters for Shorten to explain
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (12:43am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               <a href="http://www.afr.com/news/policy/industrial-relations/bill-shortens-awu-records-lost-20150706-gi68uf">
                How unfortunate:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <i>
                 Union records detailing payments by employers to the 
Australian Workers Unions Victorian branch for four years under the 
leadership of Bill Shorten have been lost
                </i>
                <br/>
                <i>
                 The Australian Financial Review [has] been told that the union had not kept records of invoices sent to employers before 2003.
                 <br/>
                 A number of employers allegedly paid the union dues of employees to the 
AWU under Mr Shorten, who was Victorian secretary from 1998 to 2006 and 
national secretary from 2001 to 2007.
                 <br/>
                 Evidence before the commission shows the AWUs Victorian branch in 2005 
received $38,228 from builder Winslow Constructors to pay the union dues
 of 105 members. Documents seen by the Financial Review also show the 
Victorian branch invoiced Winslow in March 2004 for $30,515 to pay the 
union dues of an unspecified number of workers.
                 <br/>
                 But Winslow has told the commission the practice started in the 1990s 
before Shortens time. However, sources said no invoices are held by the
 union that cover the period from 1998 to 2002 when Mr Shorten was state
 secretary.
                 <br/>
                 It is understood the union transferred invoices to a new computer 
system in about 2003 and did not shift the old financial statements
                 <br/>
                 Questioned about the Winslow payments, Mr Shorten admitted on the ABCs 
Insiders program in June that it was entirely possible that employers 
paid the union dues of members during his time at the AWU.
                 <br/>
                 Mr Shorten is also expected to be questioned on Wednesday about $300,000
 in payments by Thiess John Holland, the joint-venture builder of 
Melbournes EastLink project, to the union from 2005.
                 <br/>
                </i>
                <i>
                </i>
               </blockquote>
               Shorten will have an interesting day tomorrow at the royal commission.
               <br/>
               (Thanks to reader Peter of Bellevue Hill.)
              </div>
              ===

              <h3>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/why_should_traitors_be_citizens_whats_the_counter_argument/" rel="bookmark">
                Why should traitors be citizens? Whats the counter argument?
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4>
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2015
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (12:12am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary">
               It seems the Prime Minister reads the public mood better than do many in the media and even some in his own Cabinet:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Fairfax-Ipsos poll found
                 <a href="http://www.afr.com/news/politics/fairfaxipsos-poll-75pc-back-pm-on-citizenship-20150706-gi5una" title=" 75 per cent of people would support removing citizenship from citizens involved in terrorism provided that person is eligible to become a citizen of another country">
                  75 per cent of people would support removing citizenship from citizens 
involved in terrorism provided that person is eligible to become a 
citizen of another country
                 </a>
                 . Only 21 per cent of people were opposed
                </em>
               </blockquote>
               <em>
               </em>
               <em>
               </em>
               <br/>
               (Thanks to readers Peter of Bellevue Hill and Low Profile.)

              <div class="postsummary" style="background-color: #f8f8f5; box-sizing: content-box; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; margin: 2px 8px;">
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                It isnt often that a Fairfax environment writer comes up with the funniest line of the week. Congratulations are due to Tom Arup for composing this gem:
               </div>
               <blockquote style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  The Anglican Church has told the Abbott government to change its approach to climate change, urging it to respect and base its policy on scientific evidence.
                 </i>
                </div>
               </blockquote>
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                The comic power in that paragraph is equal to several kilotons of the finest plutonium. Here we have an organisation founded on belief and faith now demanding that selected scientific opinions inform government policy. These same people think they can talk to the planets inventor just by putting their hands together.
               </div>
               <br style="box-sizing: content-box;"/>

               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/dailytelegraph/timblair/index.php/dailytelegraph/comments/brakes_a_senatorial_debate/" rel="bookmark" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; text-decoration: none;">
                BRAKES: A SENATORIAL DEBATE
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="background-color: #f8f8f5; border-bottom-color: rgb(207, 207, 209); border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1px; box-sizing: content-box; color: #aa0033; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 0.95em; margin: 0.7em 8px 1em; padding: 0px 0px 0.2em;">
               Tim Blair
               <span class="datestamp" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #616b77; font-size: inherit; font-style: italic; font-weight: normal;">
                <span class="dash" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 
                </span>
                <span class="dayname" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 Monday
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  ,
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="month" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 07
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  ,
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="year" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 2014
                </span>
                <span class="time" style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  (
                 </span>
                 4:05pm
                 <span style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  )
                 </span>
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary" style="background-color: #f8f8f5; box-sizing: content-box; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; margin: 2px 8px;">
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                The federal senate functions as a house of review, standing above the short-term interests of the lowly house of representatives. That is why senators serve longer terms than their lower house colleagues  it removes them from the day-to-day political ruck and allows them to properly consider grave policy issues.
               </div>
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                Its such a great system that it really should apply in all other areas of Australian life. For example, imagine how helpful the new senate might be in offering a thoughtful second opinion on car repair 
               </div>
               <br style="box-sizing: content-box;"/>
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/dailytelegraph/timblair/index.php/dailytelegraph/comments/brakes_a_senatorial_debate/" rel="bookmark" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;" title="Continue reading 'BRAKES: A SENATORIAL DEBATE'">
                <img alt="Icon Arrow" border="0" height="11" src="http://resources2.news.com.au/cs/network/images/third-party/blogs/images/blogassets/images_core/v2/dailytelegraph/icon_arrow_small.gif" style="border-width: 0px; box-sizing: content-box;" width="11"/>
                Continue reading 'BRAKES: A SENATORIAL DEBATE'
               </a>
              </div>

              <div class="postsummary" style="background-color: #f8f8f5; box-sizing: content-box; font-family: 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; margin: 2px 8px;">
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                Australian feminists
                <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/dailytelegraph/timblair/index.php/dailytelegraph/sexism_enabled/" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">
                 support an American sexist
                </a>
                . Returning the favour, an American environmentalist
                <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/05/us/politics/prominent-environmentalist-helped-fund-coal-projects.html?_r=0" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">
                 supports Australian coal mining
                </a>
                , much to the anguish of the
                <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                 New York Times
                </i>
                :
               </div>
               <blockquote style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  To environmentalists across Australia, it is a baffling anachronism in an era of climate change: the construction of a 4,000-acre mine in New South Wales that will churn out carbon-laden coal for the next 30 years.
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  The mines groundbreaking, in a state forest this year, inspired a veteran to stand in front of a bulldozer and a music teacher to chain himself to a piece of excavation equipment.
                 </i>
                </div>
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  But the project had an unlikely financial backer in the United States, whose infusion of cash helped set it in motion: Tom Steyer,
                  <b style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                   the most influential environmentalist in American politics
                  </b>
                  
                 </i>
                </div>
               </blockquote>
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                Billionaire Steyer is currently running an anti-carbon campaign in the US, provoking Australian bewilderment:
               </div>
               <blockquote style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">
                 <i style="box-sizing: content-box;">
                  Its gobsmacking, Philip Spark, president of the Northern Inland Council for the Environment, a nonprofit trying to stop construction of the mine, said in a telephone interview. Its amazing that such a person could have been involved in this project.
                 </i>
                </div>
               </blockquote>
               <div style="box-sizing: content-box; line-height: 1.4em; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-top: 10px; text-align: inherit;">

                <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/dailytelegraph/timblair/index.php/dailytelegraph/oily_al/" style="box-sizing: content-box; color: #164b81; font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">

              </span>
              <br/>
              <h3 style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; margin: 0px;">
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/spend_spend_spend_senate/" rel="bookmark" style="color: #de7008;">
                Spend, spend, spend Senate
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="color: #aa0033; font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/" style="color: #de7008;">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2014
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (4:22pm)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary" style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               Forget financial reform with this Senate, where the Greens, Labor and Clive Palmer rule:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 Clive Palmer has dealt a major blow to the Abbott governments deficit repair job by announcing
                 <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/federal-politics/political-news/clive-palmer-party-to-oppose-9b-saving-measures-linked-to-mining-tax-repeal-20140707-3bi5w.html#ixzz36lFm7AMa" style="color: #de7008;" title="his party will oppose more than $9 billion worth of savings ">
                  his party will oppose more than $9 billion worth of savings
                 </a>
                 measures linked to the repeal of the mining tax.
                </em>
                <br/>
                <em>
                 The Palmer United Party leader told the National Press Club on Monday he supported the removal of the mining tax but would not vote for many of the associated savings measures. These include scrapping the Schoolkids Bonus and superannuation rebates for low-income earners.
                 <br/>
                 Scrapping the Schoolkids bonus  which delivers payments of $820 per high school child and $410 per primary school student to families on Family Tax Benefit A - would save the budget an estimated $5.2 billion over four years based on figures from the Parliamentary Library
                 <br/>
                </em>
                <em>
                 Scrapping the [Superannuation Contribution Scheme ] would save an estimated $3.8 billion over four years.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
              </div>
              <span style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">

              </span>
              <br/>
              <h3 style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; margin: 0px;">
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/comments/clive_palmer_deserves_more_scrutiny_than_this/" rel="bookmark" style="color: #de7008;">
                Clive Palmer deserves more scrutiny than this
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="color: #aa0033; font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/" style="color: #de7008;">
                Andrew Bolt
               </a>
               <span class="datestamp">
                <span class="month">
                 July
                </span>
                <span class="daynum">
                 07
                </span>
                <span class="year">
                 2014
                </span>
                <span class="time">
                 (11:16am)
                </span>
               </span>
              </h4>
              <div class="postsummary" style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               The major parties dont dare attack Clive Palmer, needing his votes. So more passive parts of the media dont put him under scrutiny either.
               <br/>
               <a href="http://www.theaustralian.com.au/media/clive-let-off-the-hook-by-starstruck-media/story-e6frg996-1226979748455" style="color: #de7008;">
                Sharri Markson:
               </a>
               <br/>
               <i>
               </i>
               <i>
               </i>
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <i>
                 THE ABC and Fairfax have refused to answer questions over their failure to prominently cover court proceedings involving Clive Palmers alleged use of siphoned Chinese cash in his election campaign
                 <br/>
                 Documents filed in the Queensland Supreme Court in Brisbane on Monday show that $10 million went from the bank account into a Clive Palmer-controlled company, Cosmo Developments Pty Ltd, in August last year, but it has not yet been established where the money went next Mr Palmer has strenuously denied any wrongdoing.
                 <br/>
                 Its a story that both The Australian newspaper and Brisbanes The Courier-Mail published on the front page on Tuesday, and Sydneys The Daily Telegraph ran prominently the same day.
                 <br/>
                 Yet the ABC and Fairfax Media have not assigned journalists to investigate the issue, nor have they covered with any prominence the court proceedings brought against the resources tycoon by Citic Pacific. The Guardian has also failed to investigate the issue independently, while the commercial networks have only touched on it lightly
                </i>
                <i>
                 The Nine Networks news and current affairs director Darren Wick said there was no deliberate strategy not to cover the story and when Mr Palmer appeared in court, well be across it" Tens news director, John Choueifate, rejected suggestions that the media had rolled out the red carpet for Palmer and said his network covered the story last week as part of a package from Canberra Sevens news director, Rob Raschke, said his state bureaus had been covering the story as part of the daily political cycle over the past week.
                </i>
               </blockquote>
               Reader Peter of Bellevue Hill adds:
               <br/>
               <blockquote>
                <em>
                 To be fair, the Fin Review ran Mark Ludlows story on
                 <a href="http://www.afr.com/p/national/chinese_chase_clive_palmer_over_7tpXxtypbJ2nRNdWutRu7H" style="color: #de7008;">
                  1 July
                 </a>
                 and also featured Angus Griggs extensive piece in the weekend edition. Jessica van Vonderens story ran on Lateline on 1 July.
                </em>
               </blockquote>
              </div>

              <div class="post-categories" style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <a href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/C947/" style="color: #de7008;">
                The new morality
               </a>
              </div>
              <br style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;"/>
              <div class="postsummary" style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="215" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/S8y8Xk24CMo" width="350">
               </iframe>
               EUTHANASIA guru Dr Philip Nitschke is furious the ABC has finally pinged him for actually helping the healthy to kill themselves.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Attacked by rabid Christians &amp; journalist jackals! he tweeted last week.
               <br/>
               But you dont need to be rabid or even Christian to consider Nitschke dangerous.
               <br/>
               For 20 years Nitschke, founder of Exit International, has had largely positive coverage from a media which too often assumed hes just helping the dying and the suffering.
               <br/>
               Only now does he seem in trouble, with the Black Dog Institute, the Australian Medical Association and beyondblue publicly denouncing him.
               <br/>
               This follows the ABCs revelations last week about Nitschkes dealings with Nigel Brayley, a healthy 45-year-old Perth man whod told the doctor he did not have a terminal medical illness, yet wanted to commit suicide.
               <br/>
               (
               <a href="http://www.heraldsun.com.au/news/opinion/at-last-we-wake-up-to-dr-death-philip-nitschke/story-fni0ffxg-1226979593653" style="color: #de7008;" title="Read full article here">

               </a>

                </em>

                So why did Christine Milne holiday on an island that Malcolm Fraser likens to Nazi Germany?
               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="color: #aa0033; font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">

              <div class="postsummary" style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               WHY have the Greens  and leftists such as former prime minister Malcolm Fraser  made Sri Lanka their favourite villain?
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Is it to better pretend that boat people from its Tamil minority are genuine refugees?
               <br/>
               Is it so they can now attack Prime Minister Tony Abbott as a criminal for sending back two boats with 200 [alleged] Tamils intercepted a week ago?
               <br/>

               </a>

               </a>
              </h3>
              <h4 style="color: #aa0033; font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
               <a class="author author-andrew-bolt" href="http://blogs.news.com.au/heraldsun/andrewbolt/index.php/heraldsun/profile/andrew-bolt/" style="color: #de7008;">

               <br/>

               <a href="http://www.jewishworldreview.com/0713/glick070513.php3#.UdlWuhYgNa9" style="color: #de7008;">
                John Kerry was the personification of the incredible shrinkage of America
               </a>
               this week as he maintained his obsessive focus on getting Israel to make concessions to the Palestinians.

              <span style="background-color: white; color: #37404e; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px;">
               In a Middle East engulfed by civil war
              </span>
              <span class="text_exposed_show" style="background-color: white; color: #37404e; display: inline; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px;">
               , revolution and chronic instability, Israel is the only country at peace.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               The image of Kerry extolling his success in "narrowing the gaps" between Israel and the Palestinians before he boarded his airplane at Ben Gurion Airport as millions assembled to bring down the government of Egypt is the image of a small, irrelevant America.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               And as the anti-American posters in Tahrir Square this week showed, America's self-induced smallness is a tragedy that will harm the region and endanger the US." - Caroline Glick
              </span>

               <div class="_3dp _29k" style="display: table-cell; vertical-align: top; width: 10000px;">
                <h5 class="_1_s" data-ft='{"tn":"C"}' style="color: #333333; font-size: 12px; font-weight: normal; line-height: 16px; margin: 4px 51px 1px 0px; padding: 0px;">
                 <span class="fcg" style="color: #89919c;">
                  <a aria-haspopup="true" aria-owns="js_41" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/page.php?id=12503781721" href="http://www.facebook.com/JosephCampbellFoundation" id="js_42" style="color: #3b5998; cursor: pointer;">

              <div class="aboveUnitContent" style="background-color: white; color: #37404e; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11px; line-height: 14px; margin-bottom: 15px; margin-top: 15px;">
              </div>
              <div class="_wk shareUnit attachmentUnit" style="background-color: white; border-left-color: rgb(211, 215, 220); border-left-style: solid; border-left-width: 2px; color: #898f9c; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px; margin: 0px 0px 12px 2px; padding: 5px 0px 5px 8px;">
               <div class="_1x1" style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px;">
                <div class="userContentWrapper">
                 <div class="_wk">
                  <div class="text_exposed_root text_exposed" id="id_51d94f09b713f1f88710680" style="display: inline;">
                   <span data-ft='{"tn":"K"}'>
                    Nietzsche was the one who did the job for me. At a certain moment in his life, the idea came to him of what he called the love of your fate. Whatever your fate is, whatever the hell happens, you say, This is what I need. It may look like a wreck, but go at it as though it were an opportunity, a challenge. If you bring love to that momentnot discouragementyou will find the strength is there.
                    <span class="text_exposed_show" style="display: inline;">
                     Any disaster that you can survive is an improvement in your character, your stature, and your life. What a privilege! This is when the spontaneity of your own nature will have a chance to flow.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     "Then, when looking back at your life, you will see that the moments which seemed to be great failures followed by wreckage were the incidents that shaped the life you have now. Youll see that this is really true. Nothing can happen to you that is not positive. Even though it looks and feels at the moment like a negative crisis, it is not. The crisis throws you back, and when you are required to exhibit strength, it comes.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     From "A Joseph Campbell Companion: Reflections on the Art of Living"
                    </span>
                   </span>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>

               The Lord will satisfy your needs
              </a>
              <span style="background-color: white; color: #37404e; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px;">
               in a sun-scorched land...You will be like a well-watered garden. Isaiah 58:11
              </span>

              </h5>
              <h5 class="_1_s" data-ft='{"tn":"C"}' style="background-color: white; color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; font-weight: normal; line-height: 16px; margin: 4px 51px 1px 0px; padding: 0px;">
               <span style="color: #898f9c; font-size: 13px; line-height: 18px;">
                Radical faith in God and radical love for people are behind Saddleback's 30 yrs of non-stop growth.Both require risk-taking.
               </span>
              </h5>

              <span style="font-family: 'Trebuchet MS', Trebuchet, Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 16px;">
